during `terraform init` when the destination backend returns an error ([#38027](https://github.com/hashicorp/terraform/issues/38027))\n    43→\n    44→* stacks: send progress events if the plan fails for better UI integration ([#38039](https://github.com/hashicorp/terraform/issues/38039))\n    45→\n    46→* cloud: terraform cloud and registry discovery network requests are now more resilient, making temporary network or service related errors less common ([#38064](https://github.com/hashicorp/terraform/issues/38064))\n    47→\n    48→* stacks: component instances should report no-op plan/apply. This solves a UI inconsistency with convergence destroy plans  ([#38049](https://github.com/hashicorp/terraform/issues/38049))\n    49→\n    50→\n    51→UPGRADE NOTES:\n    52→\n    53→* backend/s3: The `AWS_USE_FIPS_ENDPOINT` and `AWS_USE_DUALSTACK_ENDPOINT` environment variables now only respect `true` or `false` values, aligning with the AWS SDK for Go. This replaces the previous behavior which treated any non-empty value as `true`. ([#37601](https://github.com/hashicorp/terraform/issues/37601))\n    54→\n    55→\n    56→EXPERIMENTS:\n    57→\n    58→Experiments are only enabled in alpha releases of Terraform CLI. The following features are not yet available in stable releases.\n    59→\n    60→- The experimental \"deferred actions\" feature, enabled by passing the `-allow-deferral` option to `terraform plan`, permits `count` and `for_each` arguments in `module`, `resource`, and `data` blocks to have unknown values and allows providers to react more flexibly to unknown values.\n    61→- `terraform test cleanup`: The experimental `test cleanup` command. In experimental builds of Terraform, a manifest file and state files for each failed cleanup operation during test operations are saved within the `.terraform` local directory. The `test cleanup` command will attempt to clean up the local state files left behind automatically, without requiring manual intervention.\n    62→- `terraform test`: `backend` blocks and `skip_cleanup` attributes:\n    63→  - Test authors can now specify `backend` blocks within `run` blocks in Terraform Test files. Run blocks with `backend` blocks will load state from the specified backend instead of starting from empty state on every execution. This allows test authors to keep long-running test infrastructure alive between test operations, saving time during regular test operations.\n    64→  - Test authors can now specify `skip_cleanup` attributes within test files and within run blocks. The `skip_cleanup` attribute tells `terraform test` not to clean up state files produced by run blocks with this attribute set to true. The state files for affected run blocks will be written to disk within the `.terraform` directory, where they can then be cleaned up manually using the also experimental `terraform test cleanup` command.\n    65→\n    66→## Previous Releases\n    67→\n    68→For information on prior major and minor releases, refer to their changelogs:\n    69→\n    70→- This allows test authors to keep long-running test infrastructure alive between test operations, saving time during regular test operations.\n  - Test authors can now specify `skip_cleanup` attributes within test files and within run blocks. The `skip_cleanup` attribute tells `terraform test` not to clean up state files produced by run blocks with this attribute set to true. The state files for affected run blocks will be written to disk within the `.terraform` directory, where they can then be cleaned up manually using the also experimental `terraform test cleanup` command.\n\n## Previous Releases\n\nFor information on prior major and minor releases, refer to their changelogs:\n\n- [v1.14](https://github.com/hashicorp/terraform/blob/v1.14/CHANGELOG.md)\n- [v1.13](https://github.com/hashicorp/terraform/blob/v1.13/CHANGELOG.md)\n- [v1.12](https://github.com/hashicorp/terraform/blob/v1.12/CHANGELOG.md)\n- [v1.11](https://github.com/hashicorp/terraform/blob/v1.11/CHANGELOG.md)\n- [v1.10](https://github.com/hashicorp/terraform/blob/v1.10/CHANGELOG.md)\n- [v1.9](https://github.com/hashicorp/terraform/blob/v1.9/CHANGELOG.md)\n- [v1.8](https://github.com/hashicorp/terraform/blob/v1.8/CHANGELOG.md)\n- [v1.7](https://github.com/hashicorp/terraform/blob/v1.7/CHANGELOG.md)\n- [v1.6](https://github.com/hashicorp/terraform/blob/v1.6/CHANGELOG.md)\n- [v1.5](https://github.com/hashicorp/terraform/blob/v1.5/CHANGELOG.md)\n- [v1.4](https://github.com/hashicorp/terraform/blob/v1.4/CHANGELOG.md)\n- [v1.3](https://github.com/hashicorp/terraform/blob/v1.3/CHANGELOG.md)\n- [v1.2](https://github.com/hashicorp/terraform/blob/v1.2/CHANGELOG.md)\n- [v1.1](https://github.com/hashicorp/terraform/blob/v1.1/CHANGELOG.md)\n- [v1.0](https://github.com/hashicorp/terraform/blob/v1.0/CHANGELOG.md)\n- [v0.15](https://github.com/hashicorp/terraform/blob/v0.15/CHANGELOG.md)\n- [v0.14](https://github.com/hashicorp/terraform/blob/v0.14/CHANGELOG.md)\n- [v0.13](https://github.com/hashicorp/terraform/blob/v0.13/CHANGELOG.md)\n- [v0.12](https://github.com/hashicorp/terraform/blob/v0.12/CHANGELOG.md)\n- [v0.11 and earlier](https://github.com/hashicorp/terraform/blob/v0.11/CHANGELOG.md)\n","numLines":90,"startLine":1,"totalLines":90}}}

{"type":"assistant","message":{"model":"claude-haiku-4-5-20251001","id":"msg_01BYACrJq6G39etUuKDWeDCw","type":"message","role":"assistant","content":[{"type":"tool_use","id":"toolu_017yn3Z2sDLzeTh6AJ773iLy","name":"Write","input":{"file_path":"/workspace/CHANGELOG.md","content":"## 1.15.0 (Unreleased)\n\n### Breaking Changes\n\n* **backend/s3**: The `AWS_USE_FIPS_ENDPOINT` and `AWS_USE_DUALSTACK_ENDPOINT` environment variables now only respect `true` or `false` values, aligning with the AWS SDK for Go. This replaces the previous behavior which treated any non-empty value as `true`. ([#37601](https://github.com/hashicorp/terraform/issues/37601))\n\n* **lifecycle**: `replace_triggered_by` now reports an error when given an invalid attribute reference that does not exist in the target resource, preventing silent failures and making resource replacement logic explicit and validated. ([#36740](https://github.com/hashicorp/terraform/issues/36740))\n\n* **state show**: The `state show` command will now explicitly fail with a non-zero exit code (code 1) when it fails to render a named resource's state, making automation and CI/CD error handling more reliable. ([#37933](https://github.com/hashicorp/terraform/issues/37933))\n\n### New Features\n\n* **Ephemeral Resources**: New `ephemeral` block for declaring short-lived resources that exist only for the duration of a single Terraform operation. Ephemeral resources are ideal for time-limited credentials, tokens, or other temporary infrastructure resources that need to be renewed during operations. Providers implement `OpenEphemeralResource`, `RenewEphemeralResource`, and `CloseEphemeralResource` gRPC methods. Example usage:\n  ```hcl\n  ephemeral \"aws_credentials\" \"temporary\" {\n    role_arn = aws_iam_role.example.arn\n  }\n  ```\n\n* **Resource Identity**: New `resource identities` state command and provider support for stable resource identity attributes. Enables providers to define canonical identity attributes (beyond just the ID field) for reliable resource matching and import operations. Use `terraform state identities` to query resource identities with optional `-id` filtering and `-json` output. ([#38001](https://github.com/hashicorp/terraform/issues/38001))\n\n* **Pluggable State Storage**: New `remote-state-storage` provider type for implementing custom state storage backends via gRPC. State store configuration can now be declared in Terraform configuration files to delegate state read/write/lock operations to provider implementations, enabling custom storage backends without modifying Terraform core.\n\n* **List Resources**: New `list` resource block type for querying and discovering existing infrastructure resources from providers. Use list blocks to enable infrastructure discovery workflows:\n  ```hcl\n  list \"aws_instances\" \"in_vpc\" {\n    filter = \"vpc_id == var.vpc_id\"\n  }\n  ```\n\n* **Action Triggers**: New `action_trigger` block within resource `lifecycle` blocks to automate responses to resource lifecycle events. Triggers can execute actions on lifecycle events: `before_create`, `after_create`, `before_update`, `after_update`, `before_destroy`, `after_destroy`, and `invoke`. Actions support conditional execution via condition expressions.\n\n* **Removed Blocks**: New `removed` block for cleanly removing resources from Terraform state without destroying infrastructure. Useful for deprovisioning resources that are managed outside of Terraform:\n  ```hcl\n  removed {\n    from = aws_instance.old_server\n  }\n  ```\n  Set `destroy = false` in the lifecycle block to preserve the actual infrastructure while removing from state.\n\n* **Terraform Test**: New `terraform test` command for automated integration testing of Terraform configurations via `.tftest.hcl` files. Test files support:\n  - Multiple `run` blocks for sequential test steps\n  - `variables` overrides per run\n  - Assertions via `check` blocks for validation\n  - Mock provider support for testing without real infrastructure\n  - Experimental: `backend` blocks in runs to persist state between test steps\n  - Experimental: `skip_cleanup` attribute to preserve state files for debugging\n\n* **Terraform Query**: New `terraform query` command for discovering infrastructure resources matching `query` blocks in configuration. Supports:\n  - Infrastructure discovery from remote providers\n  - Variable-driven queries via `-var` and `-var-file`\n  - Configuration generation with `-generate-config-out` flag\n  - JSON output for integration with other tools\n\n* **Provider Functions**: Providers can now expose callable functions via `CallFunction` gRPC method. Functions are invoked within Terraform expressions and can perform provider-specific operations like data transformation or validation. Use `terraform metadata functions` to discover available provider functions.\n\n* **Check Rules**: New `preconditions` and `postconditions` blocks on resources and outputs for validation. Pre-conditions are checked before resource operations; post-conditions are checked after. Each rule includes:\n  - `condition`: A boolean expression\n  - `error_message`: Custom error message on failure\n  Example:\n  ```hcl\n  resource \"aws_instance\" \"example\" {\n    postcondition {\n      condition     = self.public_ip != \"\"\n      error_message = \"Instance must have a public IP\"\n    }\n  }\n  ```\n\n* **Terraform Stacks**: New `terraform stacks` command for managing stacks in Terraform Cloud. Stacks group related resources and enable advanced deployment patterns. Implemented via gRPC plugin architecture with support for protocol versioning and provider-based stack operations.\n\n* **Windows ARM64 Builds**: Official Terraform builds are now available for Windows ARM64 (windows/arm64 platform). ([#32719](https://github.com/hashicorp/terraform/issues/32719))\n\n* **Variable and Output Deprecation**: New `deprecated` attribute on `variable` and `output` blocks to mark them as deprecated. When passing values to deprecated variables or referencing deprecated outputs, Terraform will emit warnings to guide users toward preferred alternatives. ([#38001](https://github.com/hashicorp/terraform/issues/38001))\n\n* **Backend S3 AWS SSO**: The `backend/s3` backend now supports authentication via `aws login`, enabling seamless integration with AWS SSO and credential management tools. Credentials are automatically resolved from AWS SDK configuration. ([#37967](https://github.com/hashicorp/terraform/issues/37967))\n\n### Enhancements\n\n* **Provisioner PowerShell Support**: SSH-based provisioners (file and remote-exec) now re-enable support for PowerShell as the default shell on Windows connections. ([#37794](https://github.com/hashicorp/terraform/issues/37794))\n\n* **Init Logging**: `terraform init` log timestamps now include millisecond precision for better diagnostics and debugging. ([#37818](https://github.com/hashicorp/terraform/issues/37818))\n\n* **Init Developer Overrides**: The `terraform init` command now skips dependencies declared in development override files, allowing use of developer overrides while installing only truly external dependencies. ([#37884](https://github.com/hashicorp/terraform/issues/37884))\n\n* **Mock Functions in Tests**: `terraform test` now allows function definitions within `mock` blocks, enabling more sophisticated mocking strategies for provider testing. ([#34672](https://github.com/hashicorp/terraform/issues/34672))\n\n* **Deprecated Attribute Detection**: Improved detection of deprecated resource attributes and blocks to provide clearer migration guidance when providers mark schema elements as deprecated. ([#38077](https://github.com/hashicorp/terraform/issues/38077))\n\n* **Backend Nil Pointer Safety**: Backend initialization is now more robust against provider errors, preventing nil pointer dereference crashes when the destination backend returns an error during `terraform init`. ([#38027](https://github.com/hashicorp/terraform/issues/38027))\n\n* **Stacks Progress Events**: Stacks command now sends progress events during plan operations, providing better UI integration and real-time feedback. ([#38039](https://github.com/hashicorp/terraform/issues/38039))\n\n* **Cloud Network Resilience**: Terraform Cloud and registry discovery network requests are now more resilient to temporary network or service errors, reducing transient failures in CI/CD pipelines. ([#38064](https://github.com/hashicorp/terraform/issues/38064))\n\n* **Stacks Convergence Reporting**: Stacks component instances now properly report no-op plan/apply results, resolving UI inconsistency with convergence destroy plans. ([#38049](https://github.com/hashicorp/terraform/issues/38049))\n\n### Bug Fixes\n\n* **cli**: Fixed crash in `terraform show -json` when a plan contains ephemeral resources with preconditions or postconditions. The JSON output now correctly serializes ephemeral resource information. ([#37834](https://github.com/hashicorp/terraform/issues/37834))\n\n* **cli**: Fixed `terraform init -json` to properly format all backend configuration messages as JSON instead of plain text, enabling reliable JSON parsing in CI/CD systems. ([#37911](https://github.com/hashicorp/terraform/issues/37911))\n\n* **apply**: Terraform now raises an explicit error if a plan file intended for one workspace is applied against another workspace, preventing accidental cross-workspace applies that could cause state corruption. ([#37954](https://github.com/hashicorp/terraform/issues/37954))\n\n* **plan**: Fixed issue where refresh-only plans could result in a non-zero exit code even when no changes were detected, making exit code semantics consistent. ([#37406](https://github.com/hashicorp/terraform/issues/37406))\n\n* **testing**: File-level error diagnostics are now included in JUnit XML skipped test elements, ensuring CI/CD pipelines can properly detect validation failures in test runs. ([#37801](https://github.com/hashicorp/terraform/issues/37801))\n\n* **backend**: Fixed nil pointer dereference crash during `terraform init` when the destination backend returns an error, improving stability during backend migration scenarios. ([#38027](https://github.com/hashicorp/terraform/issues/38027))\n\n* **stacks**: Fixed stacks component instances to properly report no-op plan/apply results, resolving UI inconsistencies with convergence destroy operations. ([#38049](https://github.com/hashicorp/terraform/issues/38049))\n\n### Performance Improvements\n\n* **Cloud Network Operations**: Terraform Cloud and registry discovery requests now include retry logic and backoff strategies for network resilience, reducing request overhead in unstable network conditions. ([#38064](https://github.com/hashicorp/terraform/issues/38064))\n\n* **State Identity Lookup**: Resource identity schema support enables providers to offer efficient identity-based lookups for resource import and discovery operations, reducing the need for full state scans.\n\n* **Ephemeral Resource Renewal**: Ephemeral resources implement efficient goroutine management with context cancellation and proper synchronization, minimizing overhead of short-lived resource lifecycle management.\n\n### Deprecations\n\n* **AWS Endpoint Environment Variables**: The `AWS_USE_FIPS_ENDPOINT` and `AWS_USE_DUALSTACK_ENDPOINT` environment variables now strictly require `true` or `false` values. Non-standard values that previously were treated as `true` will now be ignored. Update your automation to use explicit `true`/`false` values. ([#37601](https://github.com/hashicorp/terraform/issues/37601))\n\n* **Replace Trigger Validation**: Previously, `replace_triggered_by` would silently ignore invalid attribute references. This now produces an error to help catch configuration mistakes early. Update configurations to use only valid attribute references on the target resource.\n\n* **State Show Error Codes**: The `state show` command previously returned exit code 0 even on failure. This now returns exit code 1 for failures. Update any scripts that rely on the previous behavior.\n\n### Experiments\n\nExperiments are only enabled in alpha releases of Terraform CLI. The following features are not yet available in stable releases.\n\n* **Deferred Actions**: The experimental \"deferred actions\" feature, enabled by passing the `-allow-deferral` option to `terraform plan`, permits `count` and `for_each` arguments in `module`, `resource`, and `data` blocks to have unknown values and allows providers to react more flexibly to unknown values.\n\n* **Terraform Test Cleanup**: The experimental `test cleanup` command saves manifest files and state files for each failed cleanup operation during test operations within the `.terraform` local directory. The `test cleanup` command will attempt to clean up local state files left behind automatically, without requiring manual intervention.\n\n* **Test Backend and Skip Cleanup**:\n  - Test authors can now specify `backend` blocks within `run` blocks in Terraform Test files. Run blocks with `backend` blocks will load state from the specified backend instead of starting from empty state on every execution. This allows test authors to keep long-running test infrastructure alive between test operations, saving time during regular test operations.\n  - Test authors can now specify `skip_cleanup` attributes within test files and within run blocks. The `skip_cleanup` attribute tells `terraform test` not to clean up state files produced by run blocks with this attribute set to true. The state files for affected run blocks will be written to disk within the `.terraform` directory, where they can then be cleaned up manually using the also experimental `terraform test cleanup` command.\n\n## Previous Releases\n\nFor information on prior major and minor releases, refer to their changelogs:\n\n- [v1.14](https://github.com/hashicorp/terraform/blob/v1.14/CHANGELOG.md)\n- Run blocks with `backend` blocks will load state from the specified backend instead of starting from empty state on every execution. This allows test authors to keep long-running test infrastructure alive between test operations, saving time during regular test operations.\n  - Test authors can now specify `skip_cleanup` attributes within test files and within run blocks. The `skip_cleanup` attribute tells `terraform test` not to clean up state files produced by run blocks with this attribute set to true. The state files for affected run blocks will be written to disk within the `.terraform` directory, where they can then be cleaned up manually using the also experimental `terraform test cleanup` command.\n\n## Previous Releases\n\nFor information on prior major and minor releases, refer to their changelogs:\n\n- [v1.14](https://github.com/hashicorp/terraform/blob/v1.14/CHANGELOG.md)\n- [v1.13](https://github.com/hashicorp/terraform/blob/v1.13/CHANGELOG.md)\n- [v1.12](https://github.com/hashicorp/terraform/blob/v1.12/CHANGELOG.md)\n- [v1.11](https://github.com/hashicorp/terraform/blob/v1.11/CHANGELOG.md)\n- [v1.10](https://github.com/hashicorp/terraform/blob/v1.10/CHANGELOG.md)\n- [v1.9](https://github.com/hashicorp/terraform/blob/v1.9/CHANGELOG.md)\n- [v1.8](https://github.com/hashicorp/terraform/blob/v1.8/CHANGELOG.md)\n- [v1.7](https://github.com/hashicorp/terraform/blob/v1.7/CHANGELOG.md)\n- [v1.6](https://github.com/hashicorp/terraform/blob/v1.6/CHANGELOG.md)\n- [v1.5](https://github.com/hashicorp/terraform/blob/v1.5/CHANGELOG.md)\n- [v1.4](https://github.com/hashicorp/terraform/blob/v1.4/CHANGELOG.md)\n- [v1.3](https://github.com/hashicorp/terraform/blob/v1.3/CHANGELOG.md)\n- [v1.2](https://github.com/hashicorp/terraform/blob/v1.2/CHANGELOG.md)\n- [v1.1](https://github.com/hashicorp/terraform/blob/v1.1/CHANGELOG.md)\n- [v1.0](https://github.com/hashicorp/terraform/blob/v1.0/CHANGELOG.md)\n- [v0.15](https://github.com/hashicorp/terraform/blob/v0.15/CHANGELOG.md)\n- [v0.14](https://github.com/hashicorp/terraform/blob/v0.14/CHANGELOG.md)\n- [v0.13](https://github.com/hashicorp/terraform/blob/v0.13/CHANGELOG.md)\n- [v0.12](https://github.com/hashicorp/terraform/blob/v0.12/CHANGELOG.md)\n- [v0.11 and earlier](https://github.com/hashicorp/terraform/blob/v0.11/CHANGELOG.md)\n","structuredPatch":[{"oldStart":1,"oldLines":65,"newStart":1,"newLines":141,"lines":[" ## ([#36740](https://github.com/hashicorp/terraform/issues/36740))"," ","-* You can set a `deprecated` attribute on variable and output blocks to indicate that they are deprecated. Ephemeral resources are ideal for time-limited credentials, tokens, or other temporary infrastructure resources that need to be renewed during operations. Providers implement `OpenEphemeralResource`, `RenewEphemeralResource`, and `CloseEphemeralResource` gRPC methods. Example usage:","+  ```hcl","+  ephemeral \"aws_credentials\" \"temporary\" {","+    role_arn = aws_iam_role.example.arn","+  }","+  ```"," ","-ENHANCEMENTS:","+* **Resource Identity**: New `resource identities` state command and provider support for stable resource identity attributes. State store configuration can now be declared in Terraform configuration files to delegate state read/write/lock operations to provider implementations, enabling custom storage backends without modifying Terraform core."," ","-* terraform init log timestamps include millisecond precision ([#37818](https://github.com/hashicorp/terraform/issues/37818))","+* **List Resources**: New `list` resource block type for querying and discovering existing infrastructure resources from providers. ([#37884](https://github.com/hashicorp/terraform/issues/37884))","+* **Action Triggers**: New `action_trigger` block within resource `lifecycle` blocks to automate responses to resource lifecycle events. Triggers can execute actions on lifecycle events: `before_create`, `after_create`, `before_update`, `after_update`, `before_destroy`, `after_destroy`, and `invoke`. Actions support conditional execution via condition expressions."," ","-* Terraform Test: Allow functions within mock blocks ([#34672](https://github.com/hashicorp/terraform/issues/34672))","+* **Removed Blocks**: New `removed` block for cleanly removing resources from Terraform state without destroying infrastructure. Functions are invoked within Terraform expressions and can perform provider-specific operations like data transformation or validation. Use `terraform metadata functions` to discover available provider functions."," ","-* testing: File-level error diagnostics are now included in JUnit XML skipped test elements, ensuring CI/CD pipelines can detect validation failures ([#37801](https://github.com/hashicorp/terraform/issues/37801))","+* **Check Rules**: New `preconditions` and `postconditions` blocks on resources and outputs for validation. Pre-conditions are checked before resource operations; post-conditions are checked after. Each rule includes:","+  - `condition`: A boolean expression","+  - `error_message`: Custom error message on failure","+  Example:","+  ```hcl","+  resource \"aws_instance\" \"example\" {","+    postcondition {","+      condition     = self.public_ip != \"\"","+      error_message = \"Instance must have a public IP\"","+    }","+  }","+  ```"," ","-* A refresh-only plan could result in a non-zero exit code with no changes ([#37406](https://github.com/hashicorp/terraform/issues/37406))","+* **Terraform Stacks**: New `terraform stacks` command for managing stacks in Terraform Cloud.
